<header>
<div class="dg-page-header">
    <h1>
      Betting on email: How Were Reaching Hispanics via Their Inbox
    </h1>
</div>
  <div class="authors-list authors-list--inline">
        <div class="author usa-media-block">
  <img
    class="author__photo-img usa-media-block__img"
    src="/preview/gsa/digitalgov.gov/nl-redirect-2015-content/img/digit-dark.png"
    alt=""
  />
          <div class="usa-media-block__body">
            <a
              class="author__name"
              href="/preview/gsa/digitalgov.gov/nl-redirect-2015-content/authors/lmartinez/ "
              title="Posts by Leilani Martinez"
              rel="author"
              aria-label="Read more articles by Leilani Martinez"
              >Leilani Martinez</a
            >
          </div>
        </div>
        <div class="author usa-media-block">
  <img
    class="author__photo-img usa-media-block__img"
    src="https://github.com/vwales32.png?size=50"
    alt=""
  />
          <div class="usa-media-block__body">
            <a
              class="author__name"
              href="/preview/gsa/digitalgov.gov/nl-redirect-2015-content/authors/victoria-wales/ "
              title="Posts by Victoria Bitzer-Wales"
              rel="author"
              aria-label="Read more articles by Victoria Bitzer-Wales"
              >Victoria Bitzer-Wales</a
            >
          </div>
        </div>
  </div>
        <div class="meta">
          <div class="date">
            <span title="Betting on email: How Were Reaching Hispanics via Their Inbox"
              >Jun 23, 2015</span
            >
          </div>
        </div>
      </header>
      <section>
        <div class="grid-row tablet-lg:grid-gap-6">
          <div class="grid-col-12 tablet-lg:grid-col-9 tablet-lg:order-last">
            <div class="content usa-prose"><div class="image">
  <img
    src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/digitalgov/_legacy-img/2015/06/600-x-400-Smartphone-Marco_Piunti-iStock-Thinkstock-476864628.jpg"
    alt="Woman using a smartphone"/></div>
<p>Driving visitors to a destination means reaching your users where they are at.</p>
<p>In 2005, as part of the greater USA.gov marketing strategy, <a href="https://www.usa.gov/espanol/">USAGov en Espaol</a> (<em>formerly known as GobiernoUSA.gov</em>) launched an email program. These communications initially took the form of short blurbs that directed people to important site content and promoted other government information hosted by various federal agencies.</p>
<p>From disaster preparedness, to health care, to now Twitter chats and <a href="https://digital.gov/resources/">Google Hangouts</a> our email strategy aims to provide timely messages to the public via the channel of their choice.</p>
<h2 id="curating-content-and-knowing-our-audience">Curating Content and Knowing Our Audience</h2>
<p>We understood early on that we needed to improve the way we reached our audiences. And by 2005, personal email accounts had become as mainstream as Facebook accounts are today. Ten years and tens of thousands of emails later, this communication channel is every bit asand sometimes moreeffective as its modern social media counterparts.</p>
<p>Email is a great way to nurture a captive audience. Your message is right in their personal inbox. We also want to reach people anytime, anywhere: many people<a href="https://litmus.com/blog/53-of-emails-opened-on-mobile-outlook-opens-decrease-33">over 50% by some counts</a>and certainly the <a href="https://digital.gov/resources/">Hispanic community</a> are reading emails on their phones.</p>
<p>Moreover, it has helped us learn a lot about our users, how they behave, what they want or dont want, and what resonates with them. As the first government account to do email marketing in Spanish, we had a lot to learn, but we also knew that this gave us the space to do just that.</p>
<h2 id="our-strategy">Our Strategy</h2>
<p>Today, our strategy is a hybrid of promotional tactics:</p>
<ul>
<li>Manual sends on timely topics. On average, we send two to three emails a week in response to noteworthy topics, trends, and national observances.</li>
<li>Auto sends that update our subscribers about <a href="http://blog.usa.gov/">new posts on our blog for both USA.gov</a> and <a href="http://blog.gobiernousa.gov/">USAGov en Espaol</a>. These emails are sent on a daily basis.</li>
</ul>
<p>Below is an example of a manual send email sent in late May about a national recall of Takata airbags that affected many automakers. Our call to action pointed our readers to check their VIN numbers to see if they were affected. Because the tool is in English, we gave a bit more context about what this number is. We also highlighted that these repairs are at no cost to the consumer by the auto manufacturers to ensure consumers wouldnt be victims of scams.</p>
<div class="image">
  <img
    src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/digitalgov/_legacy-img/2015/06/574-x-401-Gobierno-email-spanish.jpg"
    alt="An email campaign in Spanish, using the Gobierno U.S.A. dot gov logo header."/></div>
<div class="image">
  <img
    src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/digitalgov/_legacy-img/2015/06/574-x-371-Gobierno-email-english.jpg"
    alt="An email campaign in English, using the U.S.A. dot gov logo header."/></div>
<h2 id="experiment-and-measure">Experiment and Measure</h2>
<p>We evaluate every message we send by reviewing our data. Unique open ratesboth numbers and percentageshelp us evaluate what content performed well. We know, for example, that we have a lot of visitors to our USAGov en Espaol site seeking information on immigration. We align that information with our email sends, and the open rates and click-through rates prove the value of knowing what people are interested in. At the end of every month, our internal Performance Measurement Team provides us with a detailed report of how our messages performed. This is valuable information that informs our <a href="https://digital.gov/resources/">content strategy</a> moving forward.</p>
<p>We combine the data from email behavior with data from website visits and <a href="http://www.usa.gov/phone.shtml">calls to our contact center</a>, <a href="tel:1-844-872-4681">1-844-USA-GOV1</a>. All of these factors determine what we take our time to write and send to our email lists.</p>
<h2 id="partnerships-and-opportunities">Partnerships and Opportunities</h2>
<p>Over the years, we have employed a promotion strategy that consists of highlighting resources from our sites and other government websites. But many times, agencies have reached out to us as well when they dont have an email blast system or are looking to amplify their content. This is where the perfect match is made: when a subject matter expert comes to us. Over the years we have partnered with the Federal Trade Commission, Citizenship and Immigration Services, the Department of Health and Human Services, the Commodity Futures Trading Commission, the Social Security Administration, the Department of Housing and Urban Development, and more to cross-promote our content.</p>
<h2 id="things-to-consider">Things to Consider</h2>
<p>There are numerous things to take into consideration as you explore email campaigns. Here are some key questions to explore, based on our experience:</p>
<ul>
<li>Are your email marketing writers familiar with your content strategy? Do they understand your organizations voice?</li>
<li>Will you have dedicated resources to employ a consistent communications output?</li>
<li>Will you be able to ensure quality control so messages are well-written, culturally relevant, and targeted?</li>
</ul>
<p>These are just a few of the challenges we considered, but with the right collaboration and attention to detail, we have been able move forward in confidence.</p>
<h2 id="the-foreseeable-future">The Foreseeable Future</h2>
<p>In the next few months, we will be deploying an even more cohesive bilingual experience by aiming to send emails from other agencies directly via GobiernoUSA.gov. Right now, we cross-promote and include relevant links and messages, but in the future, we hope to send full emails that were created by our partners. Well be making content marketing decisions based on what we know our audience needs: clear, timely, interesting and useful information. Well be incorporating more messaging in English about available information in Spanish, and vice versa where appropriate, <a href="https://digital.gov/resources/">targeting a bicultural and bilingual audience</a>. This includes Hispanics who prefer English, and millennials who prefer English or Spanish information.</p>
<p>We also plan to create more action-oriented emails that are more geo-specific and targeted to <a href="https://digital.gov/resources/">personas</a>. Segmentation is something were honing as a platform strategy, so that we may serve the public in the most efficient way possible.</p>
</div>

<header>
<div class="dg-page-header">
    <h1>
      HTTPS and Other Ranking Factors: What Impacts the SEO of Government Websites?
    </h1>
</div>
  <div class="authors-list authors-list--inline">
        <div class="author usa-media-block">
  <img
    class="author__photo-img usa-media-block__img"
    src="/preview/gsa/digitalgov.gov/nl-redirect-2015-content/img/digit-light.png"
    alt=""
  />
          <div class="usa-media-block__body">
            <a
              class="author__name"
              href="/preview/gsa/digitalgov.gov/nl-redirect-2015-content/authors/dmccleskey/ "
              title="Posts by Dawn Pointer McCleskey"
              rel="author"
              aria-label="Read more articles by Dawn Pointer McCleskey"
              >Dawn Pointer McCleskey</a
            >
          </div>
        </div>
  </div>
        <div class="meta">
          <div class="date">
            <span title="HTTPS and Other Ranking Factors: What Impacts the SEO of Government Websites?"
              >Sep  2, 2015</span
            >
          </div>
        </div>
      </header>
      <section>
        <div class="grid-row tablet-lg:grid-gap-6">
          <div class="grid-col-12 tablet-lg:grid-col-9 tablet-lg:order-last">
            <div class="content usa-prose"><p>Following the <a href="https://https.cio.gov/">recent OMB memo</a> that all publicly available federal websites and Web services must <a href="http://www.digitalgov.gov/2015/07/21/an-introduction-to-https-by-18f-and-digitalgov-university/">implement HTTPS</a> by December 31, 2016, Web content managers across government are considering the <a href="http://search.digitalgov.gov/blog/seo-joe-pagano.html">SEO</a> (search engine optimization) implications of the transition, among other details.</p>
<div class="image">
  <img
    src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/digitalgov/_legacy-img/2015/09/600-x-418-search-magnifying-glass-sibgat-526855245.jpg"
    alt="An image of a magnifying glass over a computer screen"/><p>sibgat/iStock/Thinkstock</p></div>
<p>In August 2014, Google confirmed that <a href="http://googlewebmastercentral.blogspot.com/2014/08/https-as-ranking-signal.html">HTTPS is a ranking signal in their algorithm</a>. But being a ranking signal and having an impact on findability are two different things. In the post, Google describes HTTPS as a very lightweight signalaffecting fewer than 1% of global queries, and carrying less weight than other signals such as <a href="https://support.google.com/webmasters/answer/6001093">high-quality content</a>. And, in October 2014, Bing found the idea of an HTTPS boost <a href="https://www.seroundtable.com/bing-https-ranking-19243.html">almost laughable</a>. SearchMetrics recently found an <a href="http://www.searchmetrics.com/wp-content/uploads/Ranking-Factors-2015-Whitepaper-US.pdf">increasing proportion of top-ranking sites use HTTPS</a> [PDF, see page 10], but its still small and rankings are attributed primarily to brand strength.</p>
<p>While there are no inherent SEO risks to implementing HTTPS, it does count as an address change and so it <a href="http://searchengineland.com/google-starts-giving-ranking-boost-secure-httpsssl-sites-199446/">needs to be done right</a>, particularly:</p>
<ul>
<li>Place <strong>301 permanent redirects</strong> from your HTTP site to your HTTPS site, and</li>
<li>Use <strong>&lt;link rel=canonical&gt;</strong> to flag your HTTPS URLs as the version of record.</li>
</ul>
<p>And there is the added benefit of better information within analytics tracking tools, as HTTPS sites do not pass referrer data to HTTP sites.</p>
<p>So, if HTTPS doesnt have much of an SEO impact, what does?</p>
<h2 id="inbound-linksyes">Inbound LinksYes!</h2>
<p>Same as it ever was, <a href="https://moz.com/beginners-guide-to-seo/growing-popularity-and-links">link building is important</a> to improve your agency websites ranking and drive traffic to it. Government websites bear relatively higher <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PageRank">PageRanks</a> due to high quality content and other factors, including the old stand-by, number of inbound links.</p>
<p>This is sometimes confused with .gov websites getting a boost, just because they are in the .gov top-level domain (TLD). I have dug, and dug, and dug, looking for evidence of this TLD boost, and the closest I could get to an answer was a <a href="http://www.stephanspencer.com/matt-cutts-interview/">2008 interview with Googles Matt Cutts</a> saying there is nothing in their algorithm that values links from sites with a .gov TLD more highly than links from other sites. My moneys on Matt Cutts version. Every major .gov site I tested had a PageRank of 8, and <a href="https://www.usa.gov/">USA.gov</a> and <a href="https://www.whitehouse.gov/">WhiteHouse.gov</a> enjoy a PageRank of 10. Meanwhile, <a href="http://www.nytimes.com/">NYTimes.com</a>, <a href="https://www.facebook.com/">FaceBook.com</a>, and <a href="https://www.yahoo.com/">Yahoo.com</a> have PageRanks of 9, and <a href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/">HuffingtonPost.com</a> scores an 8, as do <a href="http://www.buzzfeed.com/">BuzzFeed.com</a> and <a href="http://boingboing.net/">BoingBoing.net</a>.</p>
<p>And just in the past two weeks, two studies of 2015s significant ranking factors were released, from <a href="http://pages.searchmetrics.com/rs/656-KWJ-035/images/Ranking-Factors-2015-Whitepaper-US_FINAL.pdf">SearchMetrics</a> and <a href="https://moz.com/search-ranking-factors/correlations">Moz</a>. Moz stated their study found little relationship with the type of top-level domain (.com, org, etc.) and rankings in Google.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="http://www.seobook.com/archives/001792.shtml">Tip from SEOBook</a>: Link building is a long, hard process, and requires tricks very similar to traditional marketing techniqueshave good-quality, authoritative content, and get the word out in ways people will want to link to. For instance, people love lists of thingstop 10 ways to XYZ, best resources for ABC, etc.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="60h162-and-60h262-tagsyes">&lt;h1&gt; and &lt;h2&gt; TagsYes!</h2>
<p>Using <code>&lt;h1&gt;</code> and <code>&lt;h2&gt;</code> tags in your page text shows you are thinking about user experience and want your readers to be able to scan the page quickly to orient themselves and find what theyre looking for. While a similar look can be achieved with bold text and increased font size, a search engine spider isnt able to interpret this decoration consistently. <code>&lt;h1&gt;</code> and <code>&lt;h2&gt;</code> tags are a clear signal to the spider what your page is about. Thinking of a Web page as a newspaper article, <code>&lt;h1&gt;</code> indicates the headline, <code>&lt;h2&gt;</code> the section heading, and so on, down to &lt;h6&gt;.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="http://www.searchenginejournal.com/in-2014-how-important-is-an-h1-tag-for-seo/">Tip from Search Engine Journal</a>: While the impact of <code>&lt;h1&gt;</code> on rankings has diminished over time, its still an important ranking factor. Its also an important signal to search enginesand visitors arriving at your site from search enginesabout the pages content.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.greenlaneseo.com/blog/2015/02/seo-101-seo-and-multiple-h1-tags/">Tip from Greenlane</a>: Conventional wisdom was to have only one <code>&lt;h1&gt;</code> per page, but as long as they work in the context of the page, multiple <code>&lt;h1&gt;</code> tags can be used.</li>
<li><a href="http://webaim.org/techniques/semanticstructure/">Tip from WebAIM</a>: HTML heading tags are important for 508 compliance, so screen readers and other assistive technologieswhich largely ignore visual stylingcan determine a pages information structure.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="60title62-tagsyes">&lt;title&gt; TagsYes!</h2>
<p>The <a href="http://www.digitalgov.gov/2014/03/28/plain-language-page-titles-more-important-than-ever/">&lt;title&gt; tag</a> were talking about here is located within the <code>&lt;head&gt;</code> of the page and is important for user experience on a search results page. While its basically invisible to the reader, search engines will try to use this tag for the title they display in their search results. Web browsers will display the <code>&lt;title&gt;</code> as the browser window label or tab label, and many agencies have placed a general agency, division, or site section name here, aiming to best identify the open window/tab as belonging to them. However, if all a sites <code>&lt;title&gt;</code> tags are identical, search engines wont be able to use them, and so will look to other references to your pages title to assemble something usable for their search results. The outcome of this <a href="https://blogs.bing.com/webmaster/2014/06/23/how-does-bing-choose-the-title-for-my-web-page/">page-title crowdsourcing</a> can be annoying at best, and inappropriate at worst. Your <code>&lt;title&gt;</code> tag will most likely match your <code>&lt;h1&gt;</code> tag.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="http://searchengineland.com/advanced-seo-learning-experiments-using-googles-title-tag-changes-example-189850">Tip from Search Engine Land</a>: Theres no magic number, but around 55 characters or less is good. Use the <code>&lt;title&gt;</code> tag to give each page a unique, meaningful, relatively brief title, with relevant keywords towards the beginning.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="meta-descriptionsyes">Meta DescriptionsYes!</h2>
<p>The <a href="https://moz.com/learn/seo/meta-description">meta description</a>, also located in the <code>&lt;head&gt;</code>, is search-engines first stop when they are indexing your site. After all, it would be easier for them to pull your description than to assemble their own snippet. But if you dont have this tag, or it doesnt reflect the content of the page, it may be ignored. You may have heard that <code>&lt;meta&gt;</code> tags are no longer useful in SEO, but it is only <a href="https://moz.com/community/q/meta-keywords-should-we-use-them-or-not">meta keywords</a> that are either ignored by search engines, or taken as a spam signal after this tag was abused by Web marketers trying to game the system.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="https://yoast.com/meta-descriptions/">Tip from Yoast</a>: Meta descriptions should be about 140 characters, like a tweet, and unique. Use active voice, relevant keywords, and include a call to action.</li>
</ul>
<h2 id="quality-contentyes">Quality ContentYes!!!</h2>
<p>Google has <a href="http://googlewebmastercentral.blogspot.com/2011/05/more-guidance-on-building-high-quality.html">emphasized for years</a> that the most important ranking factor is the quality of the content. Im not sure I believe this, given the PageRanks of federal websites are the same as Boing Boing. However, providing quality services and information to the public is the central goal of all government websites, and raising the bar on both the substance and the communication style can only be a benefit. While writing plainly can be a great challenge, effective communication is important for conducting our countrys business, and <a href="http://www.plainlanguage.gov/plLaw/index.cfm">its the law</a>. The direct benefits for agencies and the public are only magnified by the indirect benefit of SEO, allowing search engines to better leverage the content of your site, and get people to your information more quickly.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="http://www.plainlanguage.gov/howto/guidelines/FederalPLGuidelines/index.cfm">Tip from PlainLanguage.gov</a>: Think about your audience, organize, write your document, write for the Web, and test.</li>
<li>Tip from Copyblogger: <a href="http://scribecontent.com/downloads/How-to-Create-Compelling-Content.pdf">How to Create Compelling Content that Ranks Well in Search Engines</a></li>
<li>Tip from Killer Web Content: <a href="http://www.gerrymcgovern.com/first-chapter/28/books/killer-web-content">Do you have the killer instinct?</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
